Personally, I came to the class as a novice to the world of acting, and with the goal of becoming a much better actor. Having very little film or theater experience, it's tough to say where I'll implement the skills gained, but that will come with time. Nevertheless, I will give a stab at trying to explaining all that goes on in this class. It challenges you, it leaves you feeling empty inside some nights, it leaves you feeling completely transparent some nights, it leaves you feeling elated some nights, it leaves you feeling extremely frustrated some (many) nights, and it leaves you feeling at complete loss some nights. This is more than an acting class, as it bleeds into your daily life on a near constant basis. You will change as a person, your view of the world will change, and your relationship to everything around you will change. It's amazing to discover all that resides within you, and it's a never-ending journey. I was only able to take the class for 3 months while on summer break for school, but I hope to return to the class as soon as possible. Other students may be better suited to comment on all that the class has done for their acting abilities, but I have not put that to the test yet. Attendance is $250 per month, or about nine classes.\\n\\nGregg uses repetition to teach two things, primarily.\\nThe first you can learn in a few months: interplay. You pay close attention to another person\\u2019s behavior and react to it genuinely, uncensored. The other person does likewise. The resulting chain of reactions constitutes an interplay. But adults rely on words and intellect to communicate and have carefully-cultivated social filters.
